How do browsers handle quotation marks for <q> automatically?

Differences in accessibility impact between <q> and <blockquote>.

How to style <blockquote> in CSS while preserving semantic meaning. ^KWzWCFs6

Inline quotation using <q>: <p>He said, <q cite="https://example.com">This is amazing!</q></p>

Block-level quotation using <blockquote>: <blockquote cite="https://example.com/article"><p>This is a long quotation from an article.</p></blockquote> ^XLHsF0Za

<q>: Inline element, may contain text or phrasing content.

<blockquote>: Block-level element, may contain multiple paragraphs or other block content. ^Ou2bP0A1

Using <q> for long passages, which should use <blockquote> instead.

Omitting the cite attribute when attribution is required for clarity or legal reasons.

Using quotation marks manually in <blockquote> content instead of relying on semantic markup for accessibility. ^RC6khlri

<q> vs <blockquote>: <q> is inline and short; <blockquote> is block-level and used for longer content.

cite attribute: Optional, used to reference the original source. ^8aFT2RkW

HTML provides two primary elements to mark quotations: <q> and <blockquote>. The <q> element is used for short, inline quotations and automatically renders quotation marks around its content according to the browser's locale. The <blockquote> element is intended for longer, block-level quotations and semantically represents a section that is quoted from another source; it typically introduces indentation in rendering. Both elements support the cite attribute, which allows specifying a URL or reference to the source of the quotation. The quotation elements are semantic, meaning they convey meaning beyond mere styling, aiding accessibility and search engine understanding.
 ^POKT1jCO
